From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Mar  1 09:22:51 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (xitami@lists.xitami.org)
Date: Fri, 1 Mar 2002 11:22:51 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] changing ports
In-Reply-To: <001f01c1c0a8$a292e860$7ae6c518@homeuee8zi7q6e>
References: <001f01c1c0a8$a292e860$7ae6c518@homeuee8zi7q6e>
Message-ID: <1844082951.20020301112251@ukr.net>

Hello Mark,

Friday, March 01, 2002, 12:38:25 AM, you wrote:

M> ive read the FAQ about changing ports of the http and ftp server but theres isnt alot of info there on what files or where we need to edit this can someone help me out?
M> mark

//It's situated in xitami.cfg/default.cfg/basehost.cfg/_you_custom_host.cfg

// !!! You can't change xitami.cfg !!!

[Server]
    portbase=0         # e.g. 5000 for port 5080

[Lrwp]          # long-running web process 
    port=81             # Specifies the port on which the LRWP agent accepts connections. 
// use with portbase or not ?

[Ftp]
    port=21                             #   FTP port (+ port base)
    data-port=200                       #   Default data port
// I think it the bug in xitami.cfg (in WBA set as 20).

enjoy ;)


-- 
Best regards,
 dordienko                            mailto:dordienko@ukr.net

with Xitami? (I would like to stick with xitami

>1) When is the next major/minor release for xitami?

I have absolutely no idea.  Xitami doesn't have a release schedule as
such, and doesn't really have anyone with time to concentrate on its
development.  I suggest not holding your breath.

>2) What new features and/or options can we expect?  Are you taking any 
>   suggestions?  (multi-user admin would be nice)

Due to the aforementioned lack of release schedule there's no real list
of new features/options either.  GSL3 has been integrated into our
development version, but I have no idea if that'll be in the next release.  

You're welcome to make suggestions, but there's absolutely no guarentee
that they'll be in the next release unless those suggestions are
accompanied by code implementing the suggestion (and not even then if
integrating the feature to the existing development code is tricky).

Ewen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Mar  2 00:28:39 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 02 Mar 2002 13:28:39 +1300
Subject: The future of Xitami (was Re: [Xitami] PHP, Virtual Domains & New Features in Xitami)
In-Reply-To: Message from Francis Turner <francis.turner@freesbee.fr>
 of "Fri, 01 Mar 2002 23:22:53 BST." <3C7FFF3D.6050200@freesbee.fr>
Message-ID: <200203020028.NAA02033@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3C7FFF3D.6050200@freesbee.fr>, Francis Turner writes:
>Ewen McNeill wrote:
>>In message <3C7FCB0B.981AD47B@alum.rpi.edu>, evan heller writes:
>>>1) When is the next major/minor release for xitami?
>>
>>I have absolutely no idea.  Xitami doesn't have a release schedule as
>>such, and doesn't really have anyone with time to concentrate on its
>>development.  I suggest not holding your breath.
>
>What would it take to get Imatix to find the time? I assume that money 
>would be required to attract someone's attention.

The issue is, at base, that no one is working on development of Xitami
at anything even approaching full time (or really "at all" most of the
time to be honest).

The only "iMatix" contribution to Xitami at present is (a) providing the
site/bandwidth to host the Xitami site, and (b) my occassional posts
here (and those are over and above all my paid work -- there's no "paid
to support Xitami" going on here).  (There are a small number of people
who have paid for Xitami support in the past, who do get support, but
this number of people has not historically been enough to fund even a
part time developer, and it doesn't go towards, eg, paying me.)

There are basically two ways to go from here:
(a) Xitami development can be taken over by "the community" like a
    "traditional" open source project.  Everything that is needed to
    maintain Xitami is now open source as far as I remember (apart from
    the SSL support -- and that could be replicated by a skilled, 
    determined programmer in a week or two if they put their mind to it).

(b) iMatix somehow figures out a way to make money out of Xitami, so
    that it can afford to "dedicate" someone to working on Xitami.  (To
    be a practical proposition it'd need to fund at least half the time
    of a reasonably skilled developer; if it funds less than that
    they'll be given other work to do which will gradually take up all 
    their time (work expands to fill the time available).)

There has been various discussion at iMatix about ways to make money out
of Xitami so as to fund on-going development.  Xitami hasn't been used
in any major projects iMatix has done in at least the last two years;
even prior to that it was largely a "technology demo" rather than an
attempt at an independant product.  It's been rather more successful
than was originally planned.

Funding Xitami development from sales of Xitami/Pro, or commercial
licensing/support has been tried, and at least the way it's been done to
date, it simply does not provide enough money to fund more than
problem-focused development (eg, a customer has a specific problem and
that is investigated).

Unless there's some way to dramatically increase the number of
sales/support licences bought, it's not a practical model to fund
development.  Given the huge number of other webservers around,
including several being given away by people with Very Deep Pockets (eg,
IIS by Microsoft), a lot of people understandably simply use what they 
get for free.

Personally I think the only viable model to move forward is the
"community development" model, ie, reasonably sizable contributions from
non-iMatix people.  There have been some very good contributions in the
past, but not in sufficient quantities/focus to get to the point of a
new release/new features.

I should note, though, that management at iMatix HQ are not in favour of
"community-driven open source" style development, to the point where
it is likely that the public access to the "open source" CVS archive
at iMatixHQ will be removed, and access to the software limited to
occassional releases.

That isn't necessarily a problem: a "community driven" Xitami
development could be hosted somewhere else, based on what is currently
publically available.  I could possibly even host it on one of my
(personal) servers on the Internet.

The pay-for-development model could possibly be mixed with the
"community driven" model by, say, allowing people to sponsor a
particular feature (eg, offering to pay money to add something to the
program).  So people who want something in particular but aren't
developers themselves could still have a way of getting that feature.

Finally, FWIW, "half a developers time" is worth at least US$2500/month
(to the business; the developer may not necessarily be getting twice
that amount each month, but there's also all the overheads of providing
the developer somewhere to work, etc.)

If someone can think of a way to provide a regular US$2000/month or so
towards Xitami development, I'm all ears.  I'd like to see Xitami continue
to develop, but the only way to do that is for people to work on it --
and the only way to do that in the context of a business if for there
to be some advantage (eg, money) in doing so.

>Also on a somewhat related note: if I were to develop and sell a setup 
>that included xitami web server would you like a cut of the money and 
>would you then be willing to provide me or my customers with support?

This is definitely something that we can talk about.  Providing the
money can cover the costs of providing the support (give or take a bit)
it's quite probable something can be arranged.

Email me off list (ewen@imatix.com) and we can talk about it.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Mar  3 19:59:10 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 04 Mar 2002 08:59:10 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Poer 80
In-Reply-To: Message from John Lawson <lawson@telia.com>
 of "Sun, 03 Mar 2002 19:44:34 BST." <5.1.0.14.2.20020303194245.00c5a458@m1.520.telia.com>
Message-ID: <200203031959.IAA25527@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <5.1.0.14.2.20020303194245.00c5a458@m1.520.telia.com>, John Lawson writes:
>When I do a securityscan on my PC, port 80 is open.
>Is that correct or is ther any way ot hiding it and still have the Xitami 
>webserver running?

Yes.

You can run Xitami's HTTP server on another port using the portbase
option.

Then a different port will be open, and everyone who accesses your site
will need to use:

http://yoursite.example.com:portno/....

which wouldn't be terribly useful.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Mar  4 16:54:46 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Michael)
Date: Mon, 4 Mar 2002 11:54:46 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami Shutdown
In-Reply-To: <001601c1c373$b8998a10$037ba8c0@pooh>
Message-ID: <3C836086.9123.F920D3@localhost>

On 4 Mar 2002, at 6:57, Stan Schretter wrote:

> Is there a way to shutdown Xitami from within a Visual Basic Program

The answer is yes and yes.  But only one is relevent to this list.

Advanced (and off-topic for this list).  Use C++ or Delphi.  If you 
insist on VB, you can use API calls to identify and kill any running 
shell32 process.  If you are not familiar with api, this will ruin any 
social life you had hopes for and may require 2 gallons of Mountain 
Dew.

Much more simple (and slightly more relevent to this list) just 
minimize Xitami without sending it to the systray.  It's easy when
using Xitami to overlook this ability.  Now you can recognize and 
kill Xitami just like any other app on the taskbar using Sendkeys 
(or a few other standardized methods) and using only a couple 
lines of code.  

~Michael

open the file called 'AUTOEXEC.BAT' under c:\

and add this line then restart your computer

SET PATH=3DC:\Perl\bin\;%PATH%

you do not need to add any filters

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Mar  5 13:01:24 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Craig Morrison)
Date: Tue, 05 Mar 2002 08:01:24 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Intranet questions

Just wrote:
> 
> Question: Is there a way to name it to something other than localhost?

Create a hosts file and add entries for your machine(s).

> Question: If I want to install another Xitami in say PC#2 for this intranet,
> and leave PC#1's Xitami for all external calls?  how should I do it so it
> won't fight with PC#1's Xitami

Setup Xitami on PC#2 just like you did on PC#1. Since you won't be port
forwarding to it, the outside will never see it. Make sure there is a name for
PC#2 in your hosts file, use that name in the URL when trying to access the
local web-server.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Mar  5 14:26:37 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Tue, 05 Mar 2002 15:26:37 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] problem running .pl script
References: <C3B69919485CD31180680060942F8E4A034C6F77@ms0156t0.brux.rb.be>
Message-ID: <3C84D59D.8050606@freesbee.fr>

nico.debackere@axa.be wrote:

>Hi all,  I have a question !  
>
>Problem:
>When I access my start page, that contains a .pl script, I get the download
>pop-up message, asking me what I want do do with the start.pl script; open
>this file from its current location or save this file to disk !!  That's not
>what I want.  
>
Xitami will only run scripts in the cgi-bin directory or subdirectories 
of there. A file in the webpaqges directory is sent to the user ratehr 
than executed on the webserver.

If you want your default page (i.e. http://my.domain.com/ to run a perl 
script then you should probably create a redirection html file as 
default.htm (or index.htm) with contents like:
<html><head>
<meta http-equiv="Refresh" content="0; URL=/cgi-bin/myscript.pl">
</head></html>

For more advanced users:
I use a trivial xml / gsl combo because I can redirect all ovber the 
place with that - it also allows you to use a frameset with 1 frame to 
hide the new URL and makes it easier to maintain changes.

the gsl file (called relo.gsl) is below

.-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
.-
.-  Relocator
.-
.-  Written:  2001/12/12  Francis Turner
.-
.-  Redirects you to another port on the same server. Either as a 
redirect or
.-  as an embedded frame. You can call it in 2 ways: either call direct
.-    relo.gsl?r=PPP&m=C&t=TTT
.-    where PPP is the port for the redirect
.-    C is either an R for redirect or an F for frame
.-    TTT is a title used to give the frame mode a title. It is ignored 
in R mode
.-  or use as the script for a service.xml script
.-    e.g. a SWAT service redirector would look like
.-    <RELO SCRIPT='/relo.gsl'>
.-      <SERVICE NAME='Swat' PORT='901' MODE='FRAME'/>
.-    </RELO>
.-
.-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
<HTML><HEAD>
.if filename <> script
.  for service
.    mode ?= 'r'
.    if (substr(mode,0,1,) = "f") | (substr(mode,0,,1) = "F")
.      port ?= 80
.      name ?= "Relo "+ port
<TITLE>$(name:)</TITLE></HEAD>
<FRAMESET cols="*">
  <FRAME name="In" src="http://$(HTTP_HOST:lower):$(port:)/">
  <NOFRAMES>
  <H1>Sorry!</H1>
  <H3>This page must be viewed by a browser that is capable of viewing 
frames.</H3>
  </NOFRAMES>
</FRAMESET></HTML>
.    else
  <meta http-equiv="Refresh" content="0; 
URL=http://$(HTTP_HOST:lower):$(port:)/"></HEAD>
  <BODY></BODY></HTML>
.-  <BODY>$(port?:)=$(name?:)=$(mode?:)-$(substr(mode,0,,1):)
.- </BODY></HTML>
.    endif
.  endfor
.elsif defined(p)
.  m ?= 'r'
.  if substr(m,0,1,) = 'r'
<meta http-equiv="Refresh" content="0; 
URL=http://$(HTTP_HOST:lower):$(p:)/"></HEAD>
<BODY></BODY></HTML>
.  else
.    .t ?= "Relo "+p
<TITLE>$(t:)</TITLE></HEAD>
<FRAMESET cols="*">
  <FRAME name="In" src="http://$(HTTP_HOST:lower):$(p:)/">
  <NOFRAMES>
  <H1>Sorry!</H1>
  <H3>This page must be viewed by a browser that is capable of viewing 
frames.</H3>
  </NOFRAMES>
</FRAMESET></HTML>
.  endif
.else
</HEAD><BODY>Bad Boy</BODY></HTML>
.endif

Yes...
<snip from faq>
27: How do I use a CGI program as a default page?
    Add the index.cgi file to the list of default pages.
    Make sure that index.cgi is 'executable'.
    Define the server:cgi-url as "/".
    Define the server:cgi-bin directory to be same as server:webpages.
    Define cgi:mixed-url to be 1.
    Define cgi:dirlist to be 1 if you want directory listings to be enabled.
</snip>
Vance

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Mar  5 20:54:45 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)

Subject: Re[2]: [Xitami] Intranet questions
In-Reply-To: <OE15qUarve1WqkBpdFf0001ad8c@hotmail.com>
References: <2C61CCE8A870D211A523080009B94E430718D254@HQ5>
 <OE42jdvqyNKki1h2LKP0001aab9@hotmail.com> <3C84C1A4.5083F528@2cah.com>
 <OE15qUarve1WqkBpdFf0001ad8c@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <190606332590.20020305155445@rci.rutgers.edu>

> how to create a host file?

You surely already have one.

On my XP box it is at C:\WINDOWS\system32\drivers\etc\hosts

Win9x is different. Start, Find (or Search), Files, "hosts".

There may be hosts.sam and lmhosts. In rare cases there is no hosts
file, just the lmhosts (which is for Windows Networking). Copy one
of those, edit, save as "hosts".

Open it in NotePad. It has some comments (marked by "#") and then a
list of IP numbers and machines. Here's the default:

 #      102.54.94.97     rhino.acme.com          # source server
 #       38.25.63.10     x.acme.com              # x client host
 127.0.0.1       localhost

The acme.com entries are bogus examples, and because of the "#" are
ignored.

The "127.0.0.1 localhost" entry is how your machine finds
"localhost".

Add some lines like

 127.0.0.2  bedroom
 127.0.0.3  kitchen
 127.0.0.4  attic

Use the IP numbers you or your router assigned to your in-house
machines. Most routers use a 168... range instead of the 127...
range.

Save the file (and be sure NotePad doesn't stick a TXT extension on
it!).

On the same machine, now "http://kitchen" should open the web server
on the machine 127.0.0.3

So that every machine in the house knows the name-IP assignments for
all the other machines, copy your custom HOSTS file to the right
folder on every machine in the house.

If you let your router do DCHP, each machine's IP number may change
at each re-boot. That's no good for a static hosts file. Tell your
router to reserve some fixed IP numbers for those machines that will
have "public" (in-house) names and services, or turn off DCHP on
those machines and hand-enter IP numbers (being sure the router is
told not to use those numbers in DCHP for other machines).

That HOSTS file is how we used to do it. Much better than a printout
tacked to the wall and typing IP numbers by hand. When the ARPAnet
was dozens of machines, it was cool. But in bigger networks, it gets
cumbersome to keep adding new machines to the file and copying the
file to all other machines. ARPAnet choked when there were thousands
of machines on the net and these HOSTS files had to be updated and
distributed nightly.

That's where DNS is better. One machine holds all the data and other
machines ask it to look-up IP numbers for names they don't know. You
could set up your own in-house DNS service, but it is really more
work than a typical home LAN justifies, especially if there are only
a few machines that need to be "known" to others as DNS names.

 -PRR

I adapted to my application works flawlessly, th only bug Ive seen was if the

coming back.  There was a patch that fixed this problem and its not in the latest
release.  As far as locking up Ive not seen this.  Are you using the visual basic
framework from the xitami/addons directory?

-Joe

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Mar  6 00:10:58 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Tue, 5 Mar 2002 19:10:58 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami FTP?
In-Reply-To: <12be01c1c4a1$3b081a10$020aa8c0@Master>
References: <12be01c1c4a1$3b081a10$020aa8c0@Master>
Message-ID: <32618105699.20020305191058@rci.rutgers.edu>

> does Xitami come with any kind of "upload" engine or a feature
>that allows users to connect to the server via FTP (in a browser
>format)???

Dead-easy.

Internet Explorer works. It may work better in later versions; I
have 6 here. NetScape 4.7 works too.

ftp://username@server.domain.org

You will be promoted for your password. There is a way to give the
password in the URL; and IE also offers to save your password
locally. I prefer to keep it to myself and type it in, but whatever
works for your users.

If it likes your name and password, you can navigate folders, view
files, etc.

AND... open a File Explorer window, find files on your own PC, and
drag them into the browser window. IE just uploads them; NS asks if
that's what you want to do.

Working fine on my Xitami 2.4 server. I know I never had any file
upload add-ons.

Xitami's FTP will time-out after some minutes. I'm not sure all
browsers handle this gracefully. Best to know what you want to do
and do it all in one sitting.

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Mar  6 10:42:56 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 06 Mar 2002 23:42:56 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] LRWP help
In-Reply-To: Message from "Stan Schretter" <schrette@verizon.net>
 of "Tue, 05 Mar 2002 18:54:09 CDT." <003501c1c4a1$0b0e7480$037ba8c0@pooh>
Message-ID: <200203061042.XAA13191@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <003501c1c4a1$0b0e7480$037ba8c0@pooh>, "Stan Schretter" writes:
>I am using an  LRWP connection to Xitami from a Visual Basic program. All
>seems to work OK most of the time, but occasionally it seems that the Xitami
>server locks up and doesn't send anything over the inerface. Needs to be
>manually reset. Possibly the TCP connection is hung.

Chances are really strong that your LRWP program isn't "playing by the
protocol" in some respect, and what you're seeing is a deadlock rather
than a hung TCP connection.  You might want to double check your code is
sending the right amounts for each thing, and at least as
importantly that it's being flushed out to the network not buffered
somewhere.

Network sniffing/snooping can be very valuable in debugging this type of
issue.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Mar  6 22:46:22 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Wed, 6 Mar 2002 17:46:22 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] RE: multiple domains
In-Reply-To: <853CE5E8344DD41198B900508BD6BC90671F6E@DMNTEXCH>
References: <853CE5E8344DD41198B900508BD6BC90671F6E@DMNTEXCH>
Message-ID: <76699430377.20020306174622@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Can I run www.four-banger.net and www.mrhymbaugh.com from the same
> computer with xitami?  These are two completely different sites.
> Right now they are both going to the same site.

Register both names with your DNS, to the same machine. I think you
already have that working.

In Xitami's web-administration screen, click "V-Host Wizard". Click
"New".

Make up a name for the config file. Leave IP address blank; put
"www.mrhymbaugh.com" in "...DNS host name:".

"Web page root directory:" is the folder where this site's home page
is.

While the docs suggest that a relative path can work, I've had best
luck using an absolute path like "d:/wwwroot/Imlc". Use the forward
slashes, this isn't DOS. If you were on unix, you'd use the exact
letter-case.

For starters, you can ignore all else. Save Save Save until you
get back to the top Admin screen.

Now, stop Xitami completely, freshen your coffee, and restart it.
That isn't supposed to be necessary; X should note the modified
config file and re-read it within a minute. But some of us feel that
it is sometimes reluctant to do so. Killing it and cold-starting it
forces it to get the new configuration.

Also, whack your browser. Explorer in particular (but also NS) hates
to re-read a page if it thinks it "hasn't changed". It can't
understand that the URL is no longer supposed to go to the same
file. Leaning on Ctrl-F5 will sometimes make it go to all the
trouble of actually getting the page.

Do the same for your four-banger. It can point to your main HTML
folder, or a sub-folder.

If a request comes to your machine and does not match any of the
V-Hosts you have defined, they will get Xitami's default page,
probably your Pub Crawl page. That would happen if the page were
requested by IP number instead of name (though that is very unlikely
for your dynamic IP), or super-old browsers that do not say (in the
HTTP header) where they think they are going. So be sure that page
gives them what you want, or at least nothing too dumb.

 -PRR

All I had to do was install xitami and then I install php then it
configured it for me. If u install PHP in the default directory it makes
life easier for you. ASfter that make sure you have the filter .php or
.php3 and pointing to your executable files which would be c:\php if u
installed it in there

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Mar  8 12:41:41 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 09 Mar 2002 01:41:41 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] LRWP post size limit???
In-Reply-To: Message from "Joseph Saunders" <jsaunders@caw.com>
 of "Thu, 07 Mar 2002 18:00:08 -0800." <64DB6640B57B4C4B97F5E2A7902494170AB3FD@cawhqexch01.caw.com>
Message-ID: <200203081241.BAA24479@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <64DB6640B57B4C4B97F5E2A7902494170AB3FD@cawhqexch01.caw.com>, "Joseph
 Saunders" writes:
>Im trying to post 40 megs of data through http to lrwp.  Is there a limit
>in the XItami server that limits the size of posts to lrwp processes???

It _should_ work with 2.4d9 and 2.5b5, and I'd be interested in reports
if it doesn't.  There are bugs in all the previous 2.4d and 2.5b
versions which will cause issues with return amounts > 16KB (size where
it changed from all-in-memory to spool-to-disk).

FWIW, returning 40MB from a LRWP (or CGI or whatever) isn't all that
efficient; a 40MB temporary file will be written.  It's perhaps better
to issue a redirect to the location of the file.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Mar  8 13:08:20 2002

Subject: [Xitami] LRWP post size limit???
Message-ID: <64DB6640B57B4C4B97F5E2A7902494170AB3FE@cawhqexch01.caw.com>

Ewen,

Thanks for the response.

What im trying to do is post a tar file (40 to 50 MB) to a device that has
a Xitami web server running.  The tar is used to reinitilize the device.
I can post with a regular cgibin but the post data part of the lrwp does not
all come through.

Http may seem awkward for this but it allows an upload to happen through port
port 80 which may be the only port open on some fire walls... (ftps may not be
allowed).

-Joe
Joe Saunders
Caw Networks

FWIW, returning 40MB from a LRWP (or CGI or whatever) isn't all that
efficient; a 40MB temporary file will be written.  It's perhaps better
to issue a redirect to the location of the file.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Mar  9 01:38:39 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Michael Bronder)
Date: Fri, 8 Mar 2002 20:38:39 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Creating DDNS
References: <000d01c1c6fd$9bbf0fe0$1528fea9@GregoryHart> <000901c1c707$1b84efc0$810a3f04@jayas4t3nn91rg>
Message-ID: <000e01c1c70b$23c400a0$0400a8c0@com>

I've set this up as follows:

1) open an account with zoneedit.com (or similar service) and copy the
"nameservers" from the site that holds them now (namesecure, or whoever you
bought the domain name from)

2) a service like "DirectUpdate" (directupdate.net) once installed on your
machine will notify zoneedit whenever your IP changes.

Has been working fine for me on my cable modem since I set it up a couple
weeks ago, but my IP address hasn't changed in that time either.

mb

In message <002801c1c711$36dcdc60$4700000a@zephyr>, "Paul Berg" writes:
>Just wanted to know how i would make a vhost listening on *:8080 so the =
>site on port 80 will be different from the one on 8080.

Run two copies of Xitami.

Xitami can't listen on two ports at once in a single instance.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Mar 10 07:20:35 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 10 Mar 2002 20:20:35 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] PC chrashes
In-Reply-To: Message from John Lawson <lawson@telia.com>
 of "Sun, 10 Mar 2002 07:47:09 BST." <5.1.0.14.2.20020310074454.00bd2170@m1.520.telia.com>
Message-ID: <200203100720.UAA04064@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <5.1.0.14.2.20020310074454.00bd2170@m1.520.telia.com>, John Lawson wr
ites:
>I have set up a webserver with Xitami some time ago.
>Since then (I think) my PC has started to crash aprox 1-2 a week.
>Can this be a Xitami problem?

If the _PC_ crashes (eg, Windows blue screen) it's unlikely to be Xitami
-- Xitami doesn't do anything low level enough to be causing crashes
like that.  (Although make sure that your operating system patches are
up to date, because ISTR bugs in Windows 95/98 that would cause certain
types of file requests to crash the operating system, and these can
sometimes come in from a URL.)

Generally I'd suggest making sure you've got the latest patches, making
sure there's nothing else likely to be causing the problem running, and
then perhaps reinstalling if that doesn't work.  (I've also seen PCs
"suddenly" start crashing a lot if, eg, the CPU is overheating, or the
memory has gone bad or something, so don't completely rule out hardware
issues.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

Content-Type: application/octet-stream;
	name="welcome.pl"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable
Content-Disposition: attachment;
	filename="welcome.pl"

#!perl


#
# The welcome page.  It handles the bottom frame.  Generally, it splits
# the bottom frame into two more frames - the left (navigation) and =
right (info)
# frames.
#
# It also is used to reset the cookies on the client side when the user =
logs
# out.=20
#=20

use CGI qw(:standard);

require "systemPaths";

if (param('page') eq 'menus')  {
	showMenus();
}
elsif ((param('page') eq 'search') || (param('startOver'))) {
	showFlightSearch();
}
elsif (param('page') eq 'itinerary') {
	showItinerary();
}
else {
	showDefault();
}


########################################################################=
##

#
# show the menus - the search/itinerary/home/logout menu on the left,
# and the homepage on the right.  home button is shaded.
#

sub showMenus {

	print header();
	print <<EOF;
<!--=20
 User has returned to the home page.  Since user has already logged on,
 we can give them the menu in the navbar.
 --->

<html>
<title>Mercury Tours</title>
   <!-- Frame Set -->
   <frameset cols=3D"125,*" border=3D0 frameborder=3D0>
      <!-- Navigation Frame -->
      <frame src=3Dnav.pl?page=3Dmenu&in=3Dhome name=3Dnavbar=20
            marginheight=3D0 marginwidth=3D0 noresize scrolling=3Dauto>
      <!-- Intro Frame -->
      <frame src=3Dlogin.pl?intro=3Dtrue name=3Dinfo=20
            marginheight=3D0 marginwidth=3D0 noresize scrolling=3Dauto>
   </frameset>
EOF

}

#
# start the flight search sequence...load the menu with the search =
button
# shaded...and start the flight intro page, allowing the users to =
search
# through the various flights available.
#

sub showFlightSearch {

	print header();
	print <<EOF;
<!--=20
 User has returned to the search page.  Since user has already logged =
on,
 we can give them the menu in the navbar.
 --->

<html>
<title>Mercury Tours</title>
   <!-- Frame Set -->
   <frameset cols=3D"125,*" border=3D0 frameborder=3D0>
      <!-- Navigation Frame -->
      <frame src=3Dnav.pl?page=3Dmenu&in=3Dflights name=3Dnavbar=20
            marginheight=3D0 marginwidth=3D0 noresize scrolling=3Dauto>
      <!-- Reservation Frame -->
      <frame src=3Dreservations.pl?page=3Dwelcome name=3Dinfo=20
            marginheight=3D0 marginwidth=3D0 noresize scrolling=3Dauto>
   </frameset>
EOF

}

#
# load the itinerary pages into the info frame...and shade the =
itinerary
# button.
#

sub showItinerary {

	print header();
	print <<EOF;
<!--=20
 User wants the intineraries.  Since user has already logged on,
 we can give them the menu in the navbar.
 --->

<html>
<title>Mercury Tours</title>
   <!-- Frame Set -->
   <frameset cols=3D"125,*" border=3D0 frameborder=3D0>
      <!-- Navigation Frame -->
      <frame src=3Dnav.pl?page=3Dmenu&in=3Ditinerary name=3Dnavbar=20
            marginheight=3D0 marginwidth=3D0 noresize scrolling=3Dauto>
      <!-- Itinerary Frame -->
      <frame src=3Ditinerary.pl name=3Dinfo=20
            marginheight=3D0 marginwidth=3D0 noresize scrolling=3Dauto>
   </frameset>
EOF

}


#
# This is the default page.  It gives the user two cookies. Once cookie
# is used as user information - it starts out with only a session value =
- which
# is used later on as a weak form of authentication.  The MSO cookie is =
used
# to maintain the server options as the user moves throughout the site.
# Load in the login navigation page, with the welcome to mercury tours
# homepage.
#
# If the users directory doesn't exist in MTData, it will create it,
# and all its subdirectories.  Subdirectories are used to store =
usernames
# by hash values.
#

sub showDefault {

	# create a session ID - it's just the time for now..

	$cookie1 =3D fillCookie();

	# delete any old info and get a new server option cookie
	if (param('signOff')) {
		$cookie2 =3D cookie(-name=3D>'MTUserInfo', -value=3D>"",
							-path=3D>"/", -expires=3D>'-1d');
		print header(-cookie=3D>[$cookie1, $cookie2]);
	}
	# give them a cookie if they don't already have one.
	elsif (!cookie('MSO')) {
		print header(-cookie=3D>$cookie1);
	}
	else {
		print header();
	}
=09
=09
	# Framesets can't be in the body....

	print <<EOF;
<!--=20
 A Session ID has been created and loaded into a cookie called MSO.
 Also, the server options have been loaded into the cookie called
 MSO as well.  The server options can be set via the Admin page.
 --->

<html>
<title>Mercury Tours</title>
   <!-- Frame Set -->
   <frameset cols=3D"125,*" border=3D0 frameborder=3D0>
      <!-- Navigation Frame -->
      <frame src=3Dnav.pl?in=3Dhome name=3Dnavbar marginheight=3D0 =
marginwidth=3D0=20
            noresize scrolling=3Dauto>
      <!-- Home Frame -->
      <frame src=3D$pageBase/home.html name=3Dinfo marginheight=3D0 =
marginwidth=3D0=20
            noresize scrolling=3Dauto>
   </frameset>
EOF

	print end_html();
=09
	chdir ("MTData");=09
	createDirectories() unless (-d "users");
}

#
# Utility functions to=20
# 	build the necessary file structure
#	load the server options for a cookie
#	create the actual cookie.
#

sub createDirectories {

    mkdir ("users", 0777) unless (-d "users");
    chdir("users");
    for ($i =3D 0; $i < 128; $i++) {
		mkdir($i, 0777) unless (-d $i);
    }
}

sub loadServerOptions {
	%tempOptions =3D ( "SID" =3D> time);
=09
	$ip =3D remote_addr();
	$filename =3D $ip."so";
	$filename =3D~ s/\.//g;
	chdir("MTData");
  	open (ADMINFILE, "<$filename") or return %tempOptions;
  	$query =3D new CGI(ADMINFILE);
  	close ADMINFILE; =20

  	@names =3D $query->param;
  	foreach $key (@names) {
    	$tempOptions{$key} =3D $query->param($key) unless ($key eq =
'save');
  	}
  =09
  	return %tempOptions;
}
=09
sub fillCookie {  =09
 	%options =3D loadServerOptions();

  	return cookie(-name=3D>'MSO',
                -value=3D>\%options,
				-path=3D>"/");
}

Nothing in there "should" delete files. However, this code may work
quite oddly under Windows:


sub createDirectories {
    mkdir ("users", 0777) unless (-d "users");
    chdir("users");
    for ($i = 0; $i < 128; $i++) {
                mkdir($i, 0777) unless (-d $i);
    }

If I read it right, it makes folders with names based on IP numbers,
and chmod style permissions. This would work on unix. It "should"
degrade gracefully on NT and Win9x, but you are in an area that I
think WinPerl isn't 1,000% tested.

I'm also curious how it knows where to find its files.

You haven't told us if you run Windows, or if it has been configured
correctly, or if there is a support website that we might study.

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Mar 11 23:02:22 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 12 Mar 2002 12:02:22 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] How not to show ext.?
In-Reply-To: Message from "Just" <Just40Fun@hotmail.com>
 of "Mon, 11 Mar 2002 14:50:18 -0800." <OE38zwCMVSCxhq2pNdX000061ec@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <200203112302.MAA15272@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <OE38zwCMVSCxhq2pNdX000061ec@hotmail.com>, "Just" writes:
>1. Is there a way NOT to show the page ext.? ie to show: 
>www.abc.com/home instead of www.abc.com/home.htm ?

If you make a directory called "home", then you can use:

www.example.com/home/

instead.  (And at the expense of the webserver having to tell the
browser, "hey that's a directory" you can in practice get away without
the final "/" too; there'll be a redirect to the version with the slash.)

>2. Is there a way to prevent showing the files in a directory? ie when a =
>visitor type www.abc.com/pages when "pages" is a directory?

A.  Create an index.html file, or similar, in the directory
B.  Set [Security] dirlist=0  to disable automatic directory listings

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Mar 13 15:22:14 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Wed, 13 Mar 2002 16:22:14 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami / Mozilla bug
References: <3C14D37B.4060302@freesbee.fr>
Message-ID: <3C8F6EA6.6090708@freesbee.fr>

Francis Turner wrote:

> All,
>
> I have noted (and raised at Bugzilla) a very weird bug which I don't 
> think is Xitami related - but it could be. I have no great interest in 
> installing IIS on some machine to prove that its not a Xitami problem
>
> Basically the problem is that mozilla fails to display local xitami 
> served webpages on win2k properly.
>
> See http://bugzilla.mozilla.org/show_bug.cgi?id=114415
>
> Francis
>
For those people that care. This is related to Keep-alives and is a 
xitami / Mozilla specific problem I added the following comment to the 
bug above

More infornmation.

1) I installed an Apache server to check. Apache 1.3.23 does not 
apparently have the same problem. Thus bug does not occur with
Xitami server + IE (5.5) client,
Apache server + IE (5.5) client,
Apache server + Mozilla client

only with Xitami server + Mozilla client,
 
Implication: Something is being handled incorrectly be either Xitami or 
Mozilla (under win2k as this works for win 98/ME)

2) I have occasionally seen the same behaviour on remote Xitami servers. 
But too infrequently to troubleshoot. This led me to think about what 
might be wrong and I looked at the Mozilla Debug preferences. By 
Disabling the keep alive feature in the networking section the problem 
is resolved

i.e. a prefs setting of user_pref("network.http.keep-alive", false);

Note that the related setting user_pref("network.http.pipelining", may 
be set to either true or false with no effect. it all depends on the 
keep-alive preference.

3) There is an equivalent setting in Xitami to diable keep-alives. 
Changing this has no effect. The only working solution is to change the 
preference setting in Mozilla

Summary
The combination of Win 2000 + Xitami + Mozilla (with keep-alive enabled) 
causes the bug. Change ANY of these and the bug goes away. This bug has 
occured in all versions of Mozilla from 0.9.6 up to and including the 
latest 0.9.9

Air Force base, and shot.

If you look closely you'll see the FAQ's are older than XP, by quite a
margin.  (IIRC they're older than Win2K/WinME as well; ISTR we had this
question come up a lot when they came out.)

WinXP is basically an enhanced version of Win NT/Win2K, and so Xitami
should work fine on WinXP as far as we know.

192.195.234.26 - - [13/Mar/2002:20:29:27 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist1.pl
HTTP/1.0" 200 0
192.195.234.26 - - [13/Mar/2002:20:29:59 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist2.pl
HTTP/1.0" 200 0
192.195.234.26 - - [13/Mar/2002:20:30:26 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist2.nvm
HTTP/1.0" 200 0
192.195.234.26 - - [13/Mar/2002:20:30:07 -0500] "GET /distattack/dist2.pl
HTTP/1.0" 200 0

My best guess is that Xitami is either killing processes (although I have
disabled that feature due to long-running web-based scripts I've written)
or it has hit an OS limit (total number of CGI processes allowed by a
single process).  Is this a known bug or what exactly is going on?  Any
suggestions?

My objective is to stress test up to 100 simultaneous users over a period
of 24 hours for each scripting language...but it looks like I might have to
trim back that objective unless there is another, more viable option.

Without having run into this before myself, my hunch is that there's
perhaps some race condition in Xitami between when the temporary files
are read in (from the CGIs), and when the size of the file is recorded.
In which case this would be most obvious when the load on the machine
gets fairly high (and 50 simultaneous users all running CGIs at once
would start to do that).

Is it only the log entries affected?  Or are the results that are sent
back wrong as well?

These sorts of problems are very time consuming to track down (often
debugging is a matter of staring at the source code to try to figure out
what might be causing it, changing something "likely" and trying again).

If anyone else has seen anything similar and/or has any hints about what
triggers it, it'd be useful to know.

Ewen

I've had a different problem which may have a similar cause.


One of my perl cgi programs serves multiple responses against extra path
info in the url.
Responses are all html pages. All output is as expected, I have no
problems.

Except for one response which is multiple-framed:
  One frameset / 3 frames
  Javascript - no errors known to me.
  No html code errors known to me.
  No html code framesetting errors known to me.
  Html output varies - have 15 different frameset content for same
frameset scheme.
  Minimum total frameset content 11 Kb  / maximum total frameset content
73 Kb.


Problem:
--------
- The third frame locks Xitami up - regardless of content served,
- corrupts any files ( db temp lockfiles ) being written by the
  cgi program ( it executes ) during the lockup and
- crashes the computer.
Db is simple text files - no engine - no server.


Logfiles show
-------------
- Three successive requests - one frameset, two frames. Fourth request
not there.
- Request order of frames varies and is identical in requests both from
Netscape and  Explorer.
- Different content has different frame request order.
- Both browsers trigger the crash.


So that
-------
- A different page is being served during each crash,
- a different frame of the set is being served during each crash,
- the html/Js content served is different during each crash,
- the file size being requested is different during each crash,
- and a different browser is making the request at each crash.


The only thing I have found to be in common is the fact that a third
frame is being requested.

It's difficult to reproduce the environment unless I give a few hours of
time, because I changed the third frame to a Js write from the frameset
<head> content and solved the problem for good. However, I am upset not
being able to serve a third frame from a cgi program.

I use Windows 98 on a Pentium II 64 Mb Ram and Xitami 2.4d6 to serve an
introvert website. No workload - mostly testing.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Mar 14 16:44:45 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Espen Ruud)
Date: Thu, 14 Mar 2002 17:44:45 +0100
Subject: SV: [Xitami] Http 403 error
Message-ID: <FB7624FAD451064B9C4E74A807AC70270103307A@ex2000.forus.netpower.no>

I solved it !! (tried a lot of things)

I removed the "webmask" section from the "default.cfg" file... 

The * sign (exclude all) somehow got on a single line and excluded
everybody including myself.

I had put the * sign at the end of an IP address to exclude a series of
IP's.. but when I restarted the server the line was automatic cut and
the * was placed on the last line alone. Xitami read this as "exclude
all" and effectivly shut the server down....

Bug report..... hint hint.....Ewen :)

Espen Ruud

At 05:20 PM 3/14/2002 +1300, Ewen McNeill writeth:
>Without having run into this before myself, my hunch is that there's
>perhaps some race condition in Xitami between when the temporary files
>are read in (from the CGIs), and when the size of the file is recorded.
>In which case this would be most obvious when the load on the machine
>gets fairly high (and 50 simultaneous users all running CGIs at once
>would start to do that).
>
>Is it only the log entries affected?  Or are the results that are sent
>back wrong as well?

The results are incorrect as well (that is, the logs reflect what is
returned to the client and vice versa).  Xitami isn't dropping data being
sent back to the client.

>These sorts of problems are very time consuming to track down (often
>debugging is a matter of staring at the source code to try to figure out
>what might be causing it, changing something "likely" and trying again).

I can modify the DAS for localhost use only and send you the DAS and DAC
along with the CFM, PHP, and Perl scripts (Nuclear Vision scripts would be
semi-worthless since the executable hasn't been released yet).  The DAC
isn't 100% bug-free yet (but it is close - I just pinpointed one very
elusive bug that took forever to figure out what was going on), but the DAS
should be able to withstand anything thrown at it.  Ewen, let me know if
you want a localhost version for testing Xitami.

>If anyone else has seen anything similar and/or has any hints about what
>triggers it, it'd be useful to know.

My best guess is that there could be an OS limit on the number of processes
Xitami is allowed to start.  If that is the case, it is somewhere around
100 (50 * 2) processes (XiFusion creates a process for the CFML
executable).  I'm wondering if the NT service process limit has anything to
do with this.  I would generally think processes started by services would
be separated from the service, but they could be counted as service
processes (I think 128 service processes is the default limit).  If this is
the case, a DoS/DDoS attack could easily be created to cause about 90% of
connections to Xitami servers to fail.

If a service process limit is the problem, the solution is to track if
starting the process failed, and if it did, wait a bit (.25 seconds -
controllable from the configuration files) and then try again.  If it can't
create the process for 30 seconds, then kill the client connection with a
response that the server is overloaded.


          Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@shininglightpro.com
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

 <3.0.6.32.20020313225639.00a08b98@shininglightpro.com> <3.0.6.32.20020316121453.009e1be0@shininglightpro.com>
Message-ID: <3C93D697.E536F65C@rci.rutgers.edu>

>>What O/S?

> Win2000 ...  Hope this helps!

Doesn't help me, I just thought some wiser person would know the
limits. You later suggested 128 processes which is in the
ballpark  with your observed 100 process choke-point. I don't
know the limits, but since much NT core comes from OS/2 which is
pushing 2 decades old, but MS has had fingers in it, those
numbers are not implausible. 

Just tossing off dumb ideas....

How many files are open when you choke? Aside from your program
and data files, there may be temporary files. NT seems to handle
large numbers of live files, but I've never known the limits. 

Can you test with Xitami as a non-Service process? I don't know
if that changes anything.

Can you test on a unix platform known to have larger (or at least
very different) limits on processes? Even if your spawn processes
are not available on unix, any non-trivial filter program using
similar resources (processes, file-handles) ought to suggest if
it is the O/S or Xitami.

Can you test under Apache? If it is indeed something in Xitami,
Apache should choke differently.

 -PRR

It loads so fast locally would a stall be so obvious?

Perhaps it is having a hard time loading a specific image because it 
chokes trying to decode it.  You might have an image format Opera 
struggles with.  Images can contain a multitude of sins.  

Could be java.  Could be loading an offsite image via java.  It sure 
isn't Xitami.

By process of elimination the culprit will quickly emerge.  Start 
clean and re-insert html code until Opera chokes.  Bingo.  

As a truism, all the software I write works great locally.  It's only my 
customers who have problems.

~Michael

In message <web-980150@mi-ke.org>, "mike" writes:
>I want two web server running on one computer. The first 
>one should be xitami on port 80 listening to all IP 
>addreses. The second one is a zope server running on port 
>8080 only listening to 127.0.0.1 (localhost). If there is 
>a request for the zope server (maybe 
>http:/my.xitami.server/my-zope-server from the internet

This isn't "rewriting" so much as "proxying".  Not that it matters too
much in this instance -- Xitami doesn't support doing either at present.
You could probably write a LRWP program to do something like this if you
wanted.  (Webservers like Apache support both URL rewriting and proxying
like you mention.)

Ewen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Mar 18 16:27:15 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Mon, 18 Mar 2002 11:27:15 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami, PHP and aliases
In-Reply-To: <a74svh.3vvk2nh.1@hoplaa.oojaa>
References: <a74svh.3vvk2nh.1@hoplaa.oojaa>
Message-ID: <691713483448.20020318112715@rci.rutgers.edu>

> I thought it was a good idea to also make folders called "webpages2" and "webpages3" for
my different PHP learning projects.

[alias]
cats=E:\xitami\webpages2
dogs=E:\xitami\webpages3

Aliases are sometimes helpful for simplifying URLs to static pages.

They do NOT work well for anything complicated. In this case, Xitami
knows that cats=webpages2, but PHP does not know that. There are
workarounds for some situations, but that may be too complicated or
just more trouble than is worth for your situation.

For your situation, why not just rename the webpages2 folder to
"cats"?

 -PRR

OS/2 at the time when Microsoft had their dirty fingers in it might have
had such a limitation; since BillyG threw his toys out of the pram, and
IBM continued alone with OS/2 v2 (and later Warp v3 and v4, and nowadays
v4.52; not to mention eComStation) there's been nothing like any such
limitation in OS/2.  I have seen people speak of running THOUSANDS of
threads, in many hundreds of processes, without any problems, in OS/2.

There again, if such a limitation existed in early OS/2 code (when M$
were still on-board), it may well have been carried through into WinNT
and Win2K.

Which is the only OS that supports SMP with up to 64 processors on the
x86 family?  It's not Linux; neither is it Windoze.

1.      .
When you install PHP indicate XITAMI as server, or insert in defaults.cfg next strings:

[Filter]
    .php=%your_php_path%\php.exe
    .php3=%your_php_path%\php.exe
    .phtml=%your_php_path%\php.exe

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Mar 19 21:30:41 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Fabian Bess)
Date: Tue, 19 Mar 2002 22:30:41 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami, PHP and aliases
References: <a74svh.3vvk2nh.1@hoplaa.oojaa> <691713483448.20020318112715@rci.rutgers.edu>
Message-ID: <3C97AE01.5090704@gmx.net>

Still the best way to work around this is to use name based virtual hosts. You may want to take a look into the manual on how to set them up.

The problem is that Xitami doesn't pass PHP the translated ("real") path to the files in the alias-dir but the alias path. Of course this cannot work as PHP doesn't know of the servers alias handling.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Mar 20 12:37:38 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (xitami@lists.xitami.org)
Date: Wed, 20 Mar 2002 14:37:38 +0200
Subject: Re[2]: [Xitami] Xitami, PHP and aliases
In-Reply-To: <3C97AE01.5090704@gmx.net>
References: <a74svh.3vvk2nh.1@hoplaa.oojaa>
 <691713483448.20020318112715@rci.rutgers.edu> <3C97AE01.5090704@gmx.net>
Message-ID: <17910596834.20020320143738@ukr.net>

Hello Fabian,

Tuesday, March 19, 2002, 11:30:41 PM, you wrote:

FB> The problem is that Xitami doesn't pass PHP the translated ("real") path to the files in the alias-dir but the alias path. Of course this cannot work as PHP doesn't know of the servers alias
FB> handling.

It not absolutely so.

EXPERIMENT:

1). Lets create two aliases.

defaults.cfg

         [Alias]
             Alias1=%ALIAS_PATH%\page1.php
             Alias2=%ALIAS_PATH%

2). Lets make three files.

 - test.php
 - %ALIAS_PATH%\text.txt
 - %ALIAS_PATH%\page1.php

test.php

         <HTML>
          <HEAD>
           <TITLE> READ FILE FROM ALIAS PATH </TITLE>
          <HEAD>
          <BODY>
           <CENTER>
           <?php
             als_file=fopen("http://myhost/alias/text.txt","r");
             fpassthru(als_file);
             print("\n");
           ?>
           <hr>
           <As you can see a path is converted correctly.>
           </CENTER>
          </BODY>
         </HTML>

%ALIAS_PATH%\text.text

         <B>I am a test file with alias path.<B>

%ALIAS_PATH%\page1.php

         <HTML>
          <HEAD>
           <TITLE>PHP SCRIPT WITH ALIAS PATH</TITLE>
          <HEAD>
          <BODY>
           <?php
             print("<CENTER><B>I am a php script with alias path.</B></CENTER>/n");
           ?>
          </BODY>
         </HTML>

3).     .

RUN http://myhost/test.php

         <HTML>
          <HEAD>
           <TITLE> READ FILE FROM ALIAS PATH </TITLE>
          <HEAD>
          <BODY>
           <CENTER>
         <B>I am a test file with alias path.<B>
         
           <hr>
           <As you can see a path is converted correctly.>
           </CENTER>
          </BODY>
         </HTML>

RUN http://myhost/alias1

         <HTML>
          <HEAD>
           <TITLE>PHP SCRIPT WITH ALIAS PATH</TITLE>
          <HEAD>
          <BODY>
           <?php
             print("<CENTER><B>I am a php script with alias path.</B></CENTER>/n");
           ?>
          </BODY>
         </HTML>

RUN http://myhost/alias2/page1.php !!!!!!!!!!!!!

         <!DOCTYPE HTML PUBLIC "-//W3C//DTD HTML 4.0 Transitional//EN">
         <HTML><HEAD>
         <META content="text/html; charset=windows-1251" http-equiv=Content-Type></HEAD>
         <BODY></BODY></HTML>

!!!!!!!!!!!!! IT'S NOT MY PAGE !!!!!!!!!!!!!

 (in access.log)
 
xx.xx.xx.xx  --  [19/Mar/2002:14:20:59  -0500]  "GET /alias2/page1.php
HTTP/1.0" 200 __12__

(like in mail from:"Thomas J. Hruska" <shinelight@shininglightpro.com>
subject:[Xitami] 50+ simultaneous users...)


CONCLUSIONS:

The  server  transmits  addresses  correctly,  but  script thus is not
invoked ( the Server expects some time (12 s.), and then returns empty page).


-- 
Best regards,
 dordienko                            mailto:dordienko@ukr.net

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Mar 20 14:24:09 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Wed, 20 Mar 2002 15:24:09 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] survey: the machine you run xitami on
References: <20020320140920.39060.qmail@web14913.mail.yahoo.com>

Shane Smith wrote:

>I'm just curious to see what type of machine everyone is running xitami
>on.  I want to get an old system just to host a website, but want to be
>sure it will handle it.  I'm thinking about a pentium 233 with 128 MB RAM.
> Let me know what processor, RAM, hard drive, ...etc you have.  Also, how
>many hits per day does it handle without slowing down, crashing, etc.
>
If you are planning on hosting mainly static pages the machine you are 
thinking of is sufficiently fast that your bottleneck will be the 
internet not your machine.

If you are planning on more dynamic content (i.e. CGIs perl etc) then 
your mileage will vary based on the efficiency of your dynamic content 
and how many hits are CGI vs static, but if you dedicate the machine to 
being a webserver (no mail,ftp...) then this should be quite OK for a 
site that is connected to the internet by something less than say a 
10Mbps ethernet pipe. Personally I have  run a small website including 
perl CGIs on an ancient 75Mhz pentium with 32MB memory and win95 OSR2. 
As long as it wasn't doing ANYTHING except Xitami/perl that was fine but 
it got a bit bogged down as soon as I tried to run another app.

Francis

You're not telling us what type of load you expect, if you want to 
run PHP as a CGI module, etc. This is very important information.

>  Let me know what processor, RAM, hard drive, ...etc you have. 

200MHz MMX, 96 MB RAM, cheap-o Fujitsu IDE drive, Tyan Titan Turbo 
motherboard, running NT 4 Workstation with Xitami webserver and 
Mercury/32 mailserver. Xitami and Mercury/32 takes up VERY little 
RAM. Right now, with an uptime of ten days, the total system uses 38 
MB of physical RAM.
PHP (CGI mode) is kind of slow. Compare my personal site
http://mw.9000.org/
(which uses PHP) with a HTML-only site
http://www.brandkonsulten.se/
Those two are hosted at the same machine. Initial lag for PHP parsing 
is quite noticeable.

> Also, how
> many hits per day does it handle without slowing down, crashing, etc.

This I haven't tested. It never crashes. I have had months/years of 
uptime depending on the mail server and me installing stuff. Then, 
the websites don't see very much use, only the mail server. But I 
don't think Xitami has ever crashed -- if you avoid the beta version, 
that is...

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Mar 20 17:07:45 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Wed, 20 Mar 2002 12:07:45 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] survey: the machine you run xitami on
In-Reply-To: <20020320140920.39060.qmail@web14913.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20020320140920.39060.qmail@web14913.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <691888712815.20020320120745@rci.rutgers.edu>

> what type of machine everyone is running xitami on. I'm thinking
> about a pentium 233 with 128 MB RAM.

> dual PIII 700's - ancient 75Mhz pentium with 32MB memory - 200MHz
> MMX, 96 MB RAM -  P500Mhz with 128 Ram -  P 200 mmx 96Mb

Pentiums? DUAL Pentiums?

I got into Xitami because it runs WELL (serving static pages) on a
386SX-16 with 4 Megs RAM. Inside the building I could just tell the
difference between that throw-away 386 and a Pentium running PWS.
Outside the building, most users said it was faster than most large
servers.

If you have forgotten how slow a 386SX-16 is... NetScape 3.0 took
over a minute to load a very simple page of HTML. It was an awful
machine for browsing, but a fine server.

Xitami isn't the issue.

CGI/filters can be. Until last September I was running a university
departmental site on a P-133, 32 Megs memory, filtering most pages
through a Visual Basic filter, and speed was not an issue. I don't
have a total hit-count but the top page got 50,000 hits in 3 years,
and typical visitors hit 10 pages with several to many images per
page, or thousands of files delivered per day. And it stood up fine
to the initial onslaught of CodeRed, hundreds of stupid hits per
hour.

 -PRR

This *MAY* be related to the CGI problem reported last week.

I can repeatably get a Xitami server to crash when I hit it continuously 
with WGET running at max and hitting an XML page that runs a GSL script. 
If anyone (Ewen?) is interested in the code I can provide it.

The GSL code basically opens a specific second file, parses it and 
returns a specific text block in a webpage, with the exact file and text 
block depending on the query section of the URL. Each page is on average 
a little under 2KB and until it crashes Xitami is serving up a steady 35 
pages a second which isn't bad considering all the work that has ot be done.

After a few minutes of doing this xitami either stops responding or 
actually crashes. In neither case does anything go into the log file. 
Runing Xitami on a Win2k SP2+ pro machine with 256Mb memory and 1.5Ghz P4.

FTP server, a remote access server, plus it acts as a shared drive for my

before I got a Linksys DSL Router. I restart it once every 40 days or so
just because it feels good. It runs no foreground applications.

thousands of emails a week no sweat. SOME complicated PHP applications seem
to take too long, but other complicated PHP applications blast through
rather quickly - I need to figure out why that is.

> I'm thinking about a pentium 233 with 128 MB RAM.

> I plan on running W2K pro on this machine. There will be PHP as CGI
> and possibly an FTP server as well (not xitami). I don't expect a
> ton of hits per day (< 20). I suppose a mail server is always
> possible down the road.

Xitami is hardly an issue in this case. You will however find W2K a
hair pokey at the console. I just put XP on a K6/2-400 as an
experiment, and it don't stink (after I got more than 64M RAM in it)
but it isn't a machine I'd fly every day after being spoiled by a
Celeron 1Gig. I ran W2K on P-200 for a short time and it didn't stink,
just not as snappy as newer CPUs.

But I've run Xitami on 386SX-16 and 486-33. Installation seemed to
take forever on the 386, and slogging around NT4 on a souped-up 486
demands calm patience, but Xitami flew fine and fast.

The MP3 files should not be an issue unless you use a bloated MP3
server. Audio rates are no problem for modern networks or a P-233.

My mail server runs on PPro-233 and everything is "instant", but the
traffic there is too small to be a real test.

I say just do it. By the time you get enough CGI and other frills
loaded on to make any load worth frettting about, GigaHertz PCs will
be in trashbins looking for good homes.

 -PRR

Hello.
Adding WAP support is that easy, add these lines to [Mime] section of
defaults.cfg:

     Wbmp=image/vnd.wap.wbmp
     Wml=text/vnd.wap.wml
     Wmlc=application/vnd.wap.wmlc
     Wmls=text/vnd.wap.wmlscript
     Wmlsc=application/vnd.wap.wmlscriptc

That should be enough.
                         Zdenko.

Subject: [Xitami] Two webservers on one computers?
References: <20020320140920.39060.qmail@web14913.mail.yahoo.com> <5.0.2.1.2.20020320182512.00a4a0c0@190.190.190.1>
Message-ID: <001201c1d0b1$57a0f680$0302a8c0@pcpsilva>

That's the case, webmail runs on diferent port.
To simplify things for the user i just added a link on main site, like this
they don't have to type ":port".

I know this is not xitami related, but with webmail you can also run WAP,
for mail, and even build a site on it. Just add /wap/ after the port number.
Ex.: Web site -> www.mysite.com
       Webmail -> www.mysite.com:4096
       WAP      -> www.mysite.com:4096/wap/
I would like to have Wap with xitami. Like this i couls leave my mail server
just for mail.
I hope someone at Xitami is reading this :)

Paulo

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Mar 21 20:39:54 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 22 Mar 2002 08:39:54 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Connection Simulator
In-Reply-To: Message from Paul Reid <preid@rci.rutgers.edu>
 of "Thu, 21 Mar 2002 15:20:58 EST." <1371986706282.20020321152058@rci.rutgers.edu>
Message-ID: <200203212039.IAA25519@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <1371986706282.20020321152058@rci.rutgers.edu>, Paul Reid writes:
>> simulate a slow internet connection
>
>Put the files on a floppy disk, and point your browser at it.
>
>That's not an exact measurement. But if it sucks from floppy, it
>will suck on modem.

This isn't a bad "first cut" metric.  Floppy drives tend to get
30-50KB/second, which is roughly equivilent to a slow ADSL or cable modem 
link (say, one up to 512Kbps).  

You need to make sure the floppy isn't cached though; so write them to
floppy on one machine, and then test it on another one, to be sure.

As someone else mentioned there is some traffic shaping code in the
Xitami 2.5 beta that you could try.  Some operating systems, such as
FreeBSD (and IIRC recent Linux kernels) also have traffic shaping code.
A friend of mine used the FreeBSD traffic shaping to test one large
website for "modem speed" to good effect.

Don't forget the KISS solution -- grab a PC with a modem, dial out to
the Internet, and then try it :-)  (This is also useful for checking
that you didn't accidentally include any links that only work
internally.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Mar 25 15:48:33 2002

ok people... i must really be stupid because i am really having a tough time
figuring this out. the answers i've been given sound really simple. so can
some one give me some specifics...

problem - i have and intranet for the company. currently it is open to the
internet. i want all employees to be able to access it. the problem is that
i want to restrict public access to the site by using passwords. people in
the office should be able to access the site as normal (no password prompt),
but people accessing it from the internet should be prompted before access
is given.i would like to have people access the site using the same
urlregardless of their location.

the webmask command seems to only lock out ip ranges.... i want to set
certain ip ranges to be (or not be) prompted for passwords.

the solution i was given was to use 2 aliases - both point to the same data.
one protected by a webmask the other protected by passwords. i think this
would work - but then people would need to remember 2 urls... one for inside
and one for outside - right? and they would have to know which one to use
and when... (intranet.domain.com/public   intranet.domain.com/private)

the other solution i've come up with is duplicate the intranet webserver.
one inside the network and one out in the DMZ. that way 1 url, and the
correct dns entries... but i would have to make sure i kept both sites
identical and i would need another pc.

any more ideas or help?

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Mar 25 16:50:28 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Jay Moore)
Date: Mon, 25 Mar 2002 11:50:28 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] intranet security
References: <200203251044.LAA22998@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net> <040901c1d414$85ab8750$2f28a8c0@rcolmstead.com>
Message-ID: <002b01c1d41d$2b941670$12093f04@jayas4t3nn91rg>

set up a vhost to the intranet ip or intranet host name to point to the
intranet site....then go to the xitami directory, you should see .cfg and
.aut files for the stuff you just created...you can then manually edit the
vhost's .aut (usually the name you gave when you configured it, so if you
made it use local.cfg..you'd edit local.aut) and it's really simple..you can
look at aut files....or in the webadmin..change defualts.aut to whatever the
filename is and edit that way.

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 26 Mar 2002 08:03:01 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] intranet security
In-Reply-To: Message from "M. Jason Smiley" <jsmiley@rcolmstead.com>
 of "Mon, 25 Mar 2002 10:48:33 EST." <040901c1d414$85ab8750$2f28a8c0@rcolmstead.com>
Message-ID: <200203252003.IAA27953@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <040901c1d414$85ab8750$2f28a8c0@rcolmstead.com>, "M. Jason Smiley" wr
ites:
>problem - i have and intranet for the company. currently it is open to the
>internet. i want all employees to be able to access it. the problem is that
>i want to restrict public access to the site by using passwords. people in
>the office should be able to access the site as normal (no password prompt),
>but people accessing it from the internet should be prompted before access
>is given. [.....]
>any more ideas or help?

Configure two virtual hosts.  Configure one accessible from anywhere,
and one accessible only from the Intranet (by IP address ranges).  For
the one accessible from anywhere, configure it to require a password for
access.

Then tell the Intranet people to use the internal host name, and the
others to use the external host name.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Mar 25 20:55:47 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Stefan Pantazi)
Date: Mon, 25 Mar 2002 12:55:47 -0800

Hi,

You could have only one, unique URL which points to a CGI (could be
anything, console application, LRWP-based, etc) which looks at the IP of the
user and then routes the request through the CGI response which is a
dynamically generated temporary page with a refresh of 1 second pointing to
the to the appropriate URL (either public or private).
I hope this helps.

Stefan

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Mar 26 02:03:29 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Michael)
Date: Mon, 25 Mar 2002 21:03:29 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] intranet security
In-Reply-To: <DAECIFPNFLGIHMJEOGHMAEGLCBAA.spantazi@uvic.ca>
References: <003101c1d43c$dac563a0$2f28a8c0@rcolmstead.com>

On 25 Mar 2002 at 12:55, Stefan Pantazi wrote:

> Hi,
> 
> You could have only one, unique URL which points to a CGI (could be
> anything, console application, LRWP-based, etc) which looks at the IP of the
> user and then routes the request through the CGI response which is a
> dynamically generated temporary page with a refresh of 1 second pointing to
> the to the appropriate URL (either public or private).
> I hope this helps.
> 
> Stefan

Stefan is on the right track.  Redirecting by ip is easy esp when you 
are willing to use cgi and ssi.   There's no need for any time lapse 
or refresh.

Just create a simple script to redirect based upon ip.  You can 
easily redirect those outside the intranet one direction and those 
inside the intranet another direction.

I've done this a many times over the years.  I keep an example at 
http://alft.net/software/ip2block/  Obviously you create your own to 
do whatever you want.

One of the things I *really* like about (windows) Xitami is the ability 
to use simple win32 binaries with full ssi.   After years of severe 
limitations and abuse by isp's, I have complete freedom.  Xitami 
just fell out of the blue sky and blessed my computer.  Praise be!

~Michael

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Mar 26 09:32:54 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Tue, 26 Mar 2002 10:32:54 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] intranet security
References: <003101c1d43c$dac563a0$2f28a8c0@rcolmstead.com> <3C9F90A1.18021.148138@localhost>
Message-ID: <3CA04046.10506@freesbee.fr>

Michael wrote:

>On 25 Mar 2002 at 12:55, Stefan Pantazi wrote:

>>Hi,

>>You could have only one, unique URL which points to a CGI (could be

>Stefan is on the right track.  Redirecting by ip is easy esp when you 
>are willing to use cgi and ssi.   There's no need for any time lapse 
>or refresh.
>
>Just create a simple script to redirect based upon ip.  You can 
>easily redirect those outside the intranet one direction and those 
>inside the intranet another direction.
>

You can also do it using Xitami's handy built-in GSL scripting tool. 
Only possible disadvantage is that your HTML docuemtns will probably 
need to have a different extension. But the different extension and the 
addition of a few script lines at the top is all you need.

For example instead of index.htm you have index.dhtm
index.dhtm has the lines like the following tagged onto the front of it

.if defined(REMOTE_USER)
.- do some other validation if you feel like it e.g. check a cookie 
contacined in HTTP_COOKIE
.  define loginOK = 1
.else
.- Assume internal network is 10.1.1.0/24
.  if (substr(REMOTE_IP,,,7) = "10.1.1.")
.    define loginOK = 1
.  endif
.endif
.if (! defined(loginOK))
  Need to Login</TITLE>
  <meta http-equiv="Refresh" content="0; 
URL=http://$(HTTP_HOST:lower)/cgi-bin/ra/login.pl?referer=$(path_info)$(wasloggedin?:)"></HEAD>
  <BODY></BODY></HTML>
.  abort
.endif
<!-- start of  regular page -->

-- 
...if the US Government were ever to get really serious about Internet 
security, the top players in Microsoft's management hierarchy would find 
themselves handcuffed, blindfolded, led onto a tarmac within some obscure 
Air Force base, and shot.
-- Thomas C Greene (http://www.theregister.co.uk/content/55/23223.html)

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Mar 27 11:02:25 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marc Doigny)
Date: Wed, 27 Mar 2002 12:02:25 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] mercury smtp settings
In-Reply-To: <200203251614.KAA14511@mallard.propagation.net>
References: <040901c1d414$85ab8750$2f28a8c0@rcolmstead.com>
Message-ID: <5.0.2.1.2.20020327115304.01af4ec0@190.190.190.1>

This is actually a Mercury setup problem not Xitami, but since i'm also 
using mercury:

Goto Configuration, Core Module and change the name of the primary domain 
(tab general, internet name for this system).
Don't forget to enter all other domain names in Local domains, or the 
server will try to mail out messages destined for some local domain names 
and refuse some incoming mails.

Most important: UNCHECK "VALIDATION OF FROM FIELD WHEN PROCESSING MAIL" in 
Config, Core module, General.


You can also change your UA (user agent, that is your mail program) to use 
a different account whith the short domain name.
Normally mercury won't change From fields.
Mail me if you still have problems using Mercury: <marc@verfaillie.com>



Marc


At 16:14 25/03/02, you wrote:

>of outgoing mail. I would really like to have the shorter domain name go out
>in the From field. Is there a fix for this????
>
>Thank you,

use them I havent got a clue!  But I figure if youre running your companies 
intranet you alreay know about 10 million times more about this than I do :)

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Mar 27 18:46:28 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Michael)
Date: Wed, 27 Mar 2002 13:46:28 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] intranet security
In-Reply-To: <49.1ac38181.29d32b3d@aol.com>
Message-ID: <3CA1CD34.14447.1289462@localhost>

On 27 Mar 2002 at 9:03, Marie180@aol.com wrote:

> Ok, not that I know Jack about anything to do with webservers, or 
> programming......
> arent there environment variables in perl or php (an probably other types of) 
> code that you could use to detect and set a cgi in motion for different 
> connections (intranet / vs internet)?  What those variables are and how to 
> use them I havent got a clue!  But I figure if youre running your companies 
> intranet you alreay know about 10 million times more about this than I do :)

Big subject.  Depending on your point of view, using cgi, ssi and 
passing variables can be harder than doing a tax return  ;P  or 
more fun than doing a NYTimes crossword puzzle.

If you want simple, all-purpose perl scripts to plug in, searches 
using keywords "redirect ip cgi" came up with a few.  Some scripts 
are free.

I found the Xitami local help and online documentation do an 
excellent job ~ but assumes you understand the basics of cgi.  All 
the standard variables are explained.

~Michael

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Mar 28 14:04:38 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Joe Byrne)
Date: Thu, 28 Mar 2002 08:04:38 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] intranet security
References: <49.1ac38181.29d32b3d@aol.com>
Message-ID: <002001c1d661$7ff10c00$f6fea8c0@jjb>

Marie  (and generally anyone in this same situation)

>>Ok, not that I know Jack about anything to do with webservers, or
programming......

    I think you're coming at this from a very difficult point of view.
You're trying to learn how a 'specific' application handles a situation with
out first understanding how 'any' application in general works.  Its great
to start the learning process, and Xiami is as good a place to begin as any,
but you need to learn the basic first before worrying about the specifics.
Get some good books on how Internet servers work, especially HTTP (i.e. Web
servers) and on CGI.  Once you understand these things, then learn how to
use your specific tool to implement them.


--Joe

	This question comes up again and again, when in fact the PHP "InstallShield"
will automatically configure Xitami for PHP.

	So, I am not even sure why people try to manually configure it. Maybe because
they try to get the PHP zip instead of the "InstallShield" ?

	Frankly, all you need to do is keep clicking the Dialog for the PHP install.
The only gotcha now with the latest PHP is that you must edit php.ini and
re-enable PHP for standard CGI, they disabled that in the pre-configured files
for security reasons.

I am including my default.cfg

Xitami uses two files xitami.cfg for main configuration and any differences
will go into the default.cfg

I think the reason is that you can create multiple configurations without
copying the whole thing.

make sure php is working.  Go to your command line and type 

php -v

that should show you the version.

That should be it.

All you need then is go to your /xitami/webpages directory
and put your test.php file(remember to put .php)

------_=_NextPart_000_01C1D672.3EE5FC00
Content-Type: application/octet-stream;
	name="defaults.cfg"
Content-Disposition: attachment;
	filename="defaults.cfg"

#*END

[Accesslog]
    Format=""

[Errorlog]
    Format=""

[Filter]
    .php=c:\php\php.exe

[Ftp]
    Enabled=0

[Security]
    Dirlist=0

[Server]
    Default2=index.php
    Default3=default.htm

------_=_NextPart_000_01C1D672.3EE5FC00--

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Mar 28 18:34:16 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ed op Het Net)
Date: Thu, 28 Mar 2002 19:34:16 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Newbie question: Xitami and php
Message-ID: <112840722.20020328193416@hetnet.nl>

I have Xitami up and running on Windows 98 SE.
I've installed the latest distribution of php4.
Now, whenever I open a php-file (like phpinfo.php)
in my browser on the localhost-adress I receive the following message:

"Security Alert! PHP CGI cannot be accessed directly.
This PHP CGI binary was compiled with force-cgi-redirect enabled.
This means that a page will only be served up if the REDIRECT_STATUS CGI variable
is set. This variable is set, for example, by Apache's Action directive redirect. 
You may disable this restriction by recompiling the PHP binary with
the --disable-force-cgi-redirect switch. If you do this and you have your
PHP CGI binary accessible somewhere in your web tree, people will be able to
circumvent .htaccess security by loading files through the PHP parser.
A good way around this is to define doc_root in your php.ini file to something other
than your top-level DOCUMENT_ROOT. This way you can separate the part of your web space
which uses PHP from the normal part using .htaccess security. If you do not have
any .htaccess restrictions anywhere on your site you can leave doc_root undefined.
If you are running IIS, you may safely set cgi.force_redirect=0 in
php.ini."

I tried everything, but I can't get it to work, and an internet- and
faq-search didn't make me any wiser.
Can someone explain me in plain and simple English which steps I have
to take to solve this?

Thanks in advance, Edward


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Mar 28 18:56:22 2002

/xitami/domain1/htdocs

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Mar 29 07:10:21 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Norman Makoto Su)
Date: Fri, 29 Mar 2002 16:10:21 +0900
Subject: [Xitami] LRWP
Message-ID: <00de01c1d6f0$ca6a1710$dd31200a@JAZZ>

Hi, I've been developing a LRWP interface in ruby.  Glancing over the protocol
specs, it seems like LRWP is unable to support multiple requests at the same
time.  What I mean is that you must reply back to a request before handling the
next request.  This is different from fastcgi, where you can immediately go to
the next request (even while processing the current request).

Is my assumption correct?  Any suggestions?  Perhaps fastcgi is my only choice?

Thanks,

--
Norman


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Mar 29 15:00:25 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 30 Mar 2002 03:00:25 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] LRWP
In-Reply-To: Message from "Norman Makoto Su" <normsu@slab.tnr.sharp.co.jp>
 of "Fri, 29 Mar 2002 16:10:21 +0900." <00de01c1d6f0$ca6a1710$dd31200a@JAZZ>
Message-ID: <200203291500.DAA24626@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <00de01c1d6f0$ca6a1710$dd31200a@JAZZ>, "Norman Makoto Su" writes:
>Hi, I've been developing a LRWP interface in ruby.  Glancing over the protocol
>specs, it seems like LRWP is unable to support multiple requests at the same
>time.  

One request per connection, at a time.  If you need to handle multiple
requests at once just open multiple connections.  If there is more than
one LRWP of the same "name" connected, then they'll be given the
requests in either round-robin or first-free fashion (depending on the
configuration option).

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Mar 29 17:22:44 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marcio Marchini)

	A fresh install of the PHP  InstallShield should configure it all right, except
the security problem.

	Then you go to c:\winnt\PHP.ini (your windows dir) and declare this:

cgi.force_redirect = 0

	and that should work. In fact, you must have this value already in the INI,
commented out. In this case it is using the default value of 1, but you want 0.

	From this point on, you're on your own.

marcio
