From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Mar 29 17:42:47 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Russel Olinger)
Date: Fri, 29 Mar 2002 09:42:47 -0800
Subject: [Xitami] Newbie question: Xitami and php
References: <200203291101.MAA23809@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net> <1363151033.20020329175517@hetnet.nl>
Message-ID: <080f01c1d749$23b34460$020aa8c0@Master>

Ed:

I got this to work but there are a few catches:
1.  cgi.force_redirected = 0   ;;; make certain the ";" is removed from the
front of the line..
2.  All php files must go into the *./webpages directories for each of your
domains
3.  Pros/Cons of using the "doc_root" variable:
    CONS:
        1. #2 won't apply if you define it - ALL php files for all domains
must go into that directory, thus your files start to get jumbled together
and files for virtual domain "blah.com" will sit in the same directory for
another virtual domain "blah1.com".  There could possibly be a way around
this if you did something along the following (I haven't tested it though):
            PHP.INI: doc_root = /xitami/php
            Xitami blah1.cfg: [Alias Section] *.php = /xitami/php/blah1/
            Xitami blah2.cfg: [Alias Section] *.php = /xitami/php/blah2/

            You would have to manually created each virtual domain directory
reference in the /xitami/php directory - you would then also have to force
FTP paths so those domain admins could upload php files for their domain,
ONLY to their directory.  I think this might work.  You definently have to
jump through hoops though.

        2. By not defining the doc_root variable you could possibly open
your server to security risks.  The doc_root variable is designed to work
similar to the /cgi-bin URL call in xitami...forcing all CGIs to be in a
certain place outside of the webpages path.

    PROS:
        1. This is a security feature in PHP that allows you to remove the
php files from your accessable webpage tree path.  By default, an undefined
"doc_root" will allow the following paths to work:: /xitami/webpages/*.php,
or /xitami/webpages/php/*.php, OR  /xitami/domain1/webpages/*.php or
/xitami/domain2/webpages/scripts/*.php

A defined "doc_root" variable forces everything to that specific directory
but will prevent users from using PHP properties to scan your entire server,
outside of Xitami.

Hope this helps.
Russel

	I don't know how many of you are familiar with mod_backhand for the apache 
server, but it allows you to have a cluster of servers with one master 
server that handles all incoming connections.  Based on how busy each 
machine is in the cluster, backhand decides if the master machine should 
handle the request, or if it should redirect the request to another machine...

	Is there anything like this available for use with Xitami on a windows 
platform??

in the /WINNT/PHP.INI file there is a line:
;cgi.force_redirect =3D 1

Remove the ";" from the front of the line and change the 1 to a 0.  This =
will allow PHP files to be accessed from the /webpages directory or any =
of its sub-directories (or what ever is your default HTML directory)

In message <xtvzr050dg8jc3s.290320021454@ken>, "kenjoy@kenjoy.com" writes:
>We're away for the weekend and will be back in the office on Sunday Morning.  
>We'll respond to your e-mail as soon as we return.

kenjoy@kenjoy.com has been unsubscribed from the Xitami mailing list
because of this persistent vacation message being submitted to the
mailing list.  At present they can still resubscribe when they return;
but if it happens again they'll be banned from the mailing list.

Please folks, if you're going to configure a vacation message:
- make sure that it doesn't go to the mailing lists you are on (or 
  unsubscribe from the mailing lists when you go away, or just set them
  to "no mail" on the webpage)
- make sure that it only sends one message to each destination in a
  long period of time (eg, once a week or something)
- make very sure it doesn't respond to messages it generated itself,
  however they get back to it.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

{ SEQ CHAPTER \h \r 1}     I run Xitami for OS/2 ( OS/2 has always run very stability for me in the past and I 
have never wanted to change from something that "worked very well" for me).  Xitami 
runs completely dedicated on it's own machine (Pentium 100 with 32 megs of ram) 
running OS/2 Warp 4.0 .  I recently upgraded my feed to a 768 SDSL net connection to 
host some original artwork.  When up and running I am expecting anywhere from 10-20+ 
simultaneous connections during normal peak usage hours.  

     I have two concerns.  One: some of those connecting will be broadband connections.  
Won't the broadband connections take the lion share of the bandwidth (being able to 
take more faster in shorter time frame) leaving the dialups with the scraps of what they 
can down feed in a bandwidth crunch?  Is there a way under Xitami or OS/2 to make 
sure everyone gets an even amount of bandwidth at peak usage (unless this is done 
normally) or throttle bandwidth per connection to a specific kb (say 8 kb) all the time?  

     My second question is I saw in the faq that EMX was limited to 40 open sockets in 
the faq.  This has been in the faq for a LONG time.  Has the newer versions of EMX 
made improvements on this?  Also is that 40 sockets per EMX application or the entire 
machine?  I'm wondering if this 40 max sockets will hit me.

     I am not opposed to running Xitami under Windows if I have to.  If possible I would 
like to stay with OS/2 as I have left it running for over a year without even so much as 
having to reset the server.  My experience with running Xitami under NT 4 was it would 
run fine for a week to a month then Xitami would suddenly stop taking connections.  But 
everything would look like it was still running fine.  However if it turns out my only option 
is to switch perhaps there are some settings that can improve reliability?

Thanks very much anyone for any information!  Gene Angel

Just one more question. Redirection worked fine after a fresh install.

php-files locally, so it's not a security issue), I have to define the
exact name of the php-file, before it works.

gives me the output of info.php.
Did I miss a configuration option in Xitami?

RO> I got this to work but there are a few catches:
RO> 1.  cgi.force_redirected = 0   ;;; make certain the ";" is removed from the
RO> front of the line..
RO> 2.  All php files must go into the *./webpages directories for each of your
RO> domains
RO> 3.  Pros/Cons of using the "doc_root" variable:
RO>     CONS:
RO>         1. #2 won't apply if you define it - ALL php files for all domains
RO> must go into that directory, thus your files start to get jumbled together
RO> and files for virtual domain "blah.com" will sit in the same directory for
RO> another virtual domain "blah1.com".  There could possibly be a way around
RO> this if you did something along the following (I haven't tested it though):
RO>             PHP.INI: doc_root = /xitami/php
RO>             Xitami blah1.cfg: [Alias Section] *.php = /xitami/php/blah1/
RO>             Xitami blah2.cfg: [Alias Section] *.php = /xitami/php/blah2/

RO>             You would have to manually created each virtual domain directory
RO> reference in the /xitami/php directory - you would then also have to force
RO> FTP paths so those domain admins could upload php files for their domain,
RO> ONLY to their directory.  I think this might work.  You definently have to
RO> jump through hoops though.
